    Miguel de Cervantes
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">

    </div>

       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       This name uses
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_naming_customs" title="Spanish naming customs">
        Spanish naming customs
       </a>
       : the first or paternal
       <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">
        family name
       </a>
       is
       <i>
        de Cervantes
       </i>
       and the second or maternal family name is
       <i>
        Saavedra
       </i>
       .
      </div>

      <p>
       <b>
        Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra
       </b>
       <sup class="reference" id="ref_Bnone">
        <a href="#endnote_Bnone">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">
            ər
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">
            eɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">
            ər
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [miˈɣel de θerˈβantes saˈβeðɾa]
        </a>
       </span>
       ; 29 September 1547 (assumed) – 22 April 1616)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was a Spanish writer who is widely regarded as the greatest writer in the Spanish language and one of the world's pre-eminent novelists. His masterpiece
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
         Don Quixote
        </a>
       </i>
       has been translated into more languages than any other book except the Bible.
      </p>
      <p>
       His major work,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
         Don Quixote
        </a>
       </i>
       , sometimes considered the first modern novel,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a classic of
       <a href="/wiki/Western_literature" title="Western literature">
        Western literature
       </a>
       , regarded among the best works of fiction ever written.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His influence on the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish language
       </a>
       has been so great that the language is often called
       <i>
        la lengua de Cervantes
       </i>
       ("the language of Cervantes").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He has also been dubbed
       <i>
        El príncipe de los ingenios
       </i>
       ("The Prince of Wits").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1569, in forced exile from Castile, Cervantes moved to Rome, where he worked as chamber assistant of a cardinal. Then he enlisted as a soldier in a
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy_Marines" title="Spanish Navy Marines">
        Spanish Navy infantry
       </a>
       regiment and continued his military life until 1575, when he was captured by
       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">
        Barbary pirates
       </a>
       . After five years of captivity, he was released on payment of a ransom by his parents and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinitarians" title="Trinitarians">
        Trinitarians
       </a>
       , a Catholic religious order, and he returned to his family in Madrid.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1585, Cervantes published a
       <a href="/wiki/Pastoral" title="Pastoral">
        pastoral
       </a>
       novel titled
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Galatea" title="La Galatea">
         La Galatea
        </a>
       </i>
       . He worked as a purchasing agent for the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">
        Spanish Armada
       </a>
       and later as a
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_collector" title="Tax collector">
        tax collector
       </a>
       for the government. In 1597, discrepancies in his accounts for three years previous landed him in the Crown Jail of
       <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
        Seville
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1605, Cervantes was in
       <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">
        Valladolid
       </a>
       when the immediate success of the first part of his
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
         Don Quixote
        </a>
       </i>
       , published in Madrid, signalled his return to the literary world. In 1607, he settled in Madrid, where he lived and worked until his death. During the last nine years of his life, Cervantes solidified his reputation as a writer, publishing
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Novelas_ejemplares" title="Novelas ejemplares">
         Novelas ejemplares
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Exemplary Novels
       </i>
       ) in 1613,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viaje_al_Parnaso" title="Viaje al Parnaso">
         Viaje al Parnaso
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Journey to Parnassus
       </i>
       ) in 1614, and
       <i>
        Ocho comedias y ocho entremeses
       </i>
       and the second part of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       in 1615. His last work,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Los_trabajos_de_Persiles_y_Sigismunda" title="Los trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda">
         Los trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda
        </a>
       </i>
       ("
       <i>
        The Travails of Persiles and Sigismunda
       </i>
       "), was published posthumously in 1617.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_early_life">
        Birth and early life
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Birth and early life">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="margin: 0 0 1em 1em; border: 1px solid #aaaaaa; background: #ffffff; float:right;">
       <tr>
        <th style="padding: 0 5px 0 5px; background:#ccccff; text-align:center;">
         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_literature" title="Spanish literature">
          Literature of Spain
         </a>
         <br/>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">
         • Medieval literature
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">
         •
         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Renaissance_literature" title="Spanish Renaissance literature">
          Renaissance
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">
         •
         <a class="mw-selflink selflink">
          Miguel de Cervantes
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

         </a>

         </a>

       </tr>

         </a>
        </td>

         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">

           Modernismo
          </i>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">

         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">

         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">

         </a>

       <tr>
        <td style="font-size: 90%; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;">
         • Literature subsequent to the Civil War
        </td>
       </tr>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capilla_del_Oidor,_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg/220px-Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg/330px-Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg/440px-Capilla_del_Oidor%2C_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capilla_del_Oidor,_Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Church of
         <i>
          Santa María la Mayor
         </i>
         where Cervantes was baptized in
         <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">
          Alcalá de Henares
         </a>
         . The square in front of it is now called
         <i>
          Plaza Cervantes
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       It is assumed that Cervantes was born in
       <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">
        Alcalá de Henares
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">
        Castilian
       </a>
       city about 35 kilometres (22 mi) north-east from Madrid, probably on 29 September (the feast day of
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">
        Saint Michael the Archangel
       </a>
       ) 1547. The probable date of his birth was determined from records in the church register, given the tradition of naming a child after the feast day of his birth. He was baptized in Alcalá de Henares on 9 October 1547
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at the parish church of
       <i>
        Santa María la Mayor
       </i>
       . The register of baptisms records the following:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        On Sunday, the ninth day of the month of October, the year of our Lord one thousand five hundred forty and seven, Miguel, son of Rodrigo Cervantes and his wife Leonor, was baptised; his godfathers were Juan Pardo; he was baptised by the Reverend Bachelor Bartolomé Serrano, Priest of Our Lady. Witnesses, Baltasar Vázquez, Sexton, and I, who baptised him and signed this in my name. Bachelor Serrano.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
         <a href="#cite_note-10">
          [10]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       Miguel at birth was not surnamed
       <i>
        Cervantes Saavedra
       </i>
       . He adopted the "Saavedra" name as an adult. By
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_name" title="Spanish name">
        Spanish naming conventions
       </a>
       , his second surname was that of his mother, Cortinas. His father, Rodrigo, was a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barber-surgeon" title="Barber-surgeon">
        barber-surgeon
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Galicians" title="Galicians">
        Galician
       </a>
       extraction
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       , who set bones, performed blood-lettings, and attended to "lesser medical needs";
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at that time, it was common for barbers to do surgery as well. His paternal grandfather, Juan de Cervantes, was an influential lawyer who held several administrative positions. His uncle was mayor of Cabra for many years. His mother, Leonor de Cortinas, was a native of
       <a href="/wiki/Arganda_del_Rey" title="Arganda del Rey">
        Arganda del Rey
       </a>
       and the third daughter of a nobleman, who lost his fortune and had to sell his daughter into matrimony in 1543. This led to a very awkward marriage and several affairs by Rodrigo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Leonor died on 19 October 1593.
      </p>
      <p>
       Little is known of Cervantes' early years. It seems he spent much of his childhood moving from town to town with his family, eventually enrolling in
       <a href="/wiki/Instituto_San_Isidro" title="Instituto San Isidro">
        The Imperial School
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       educational establishment for boys in Madrid.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this time, he met a young barmaid named Josefina Catalina de Parez. The couple fell madly in love and plotted to run away together. Her father discovered their plans and forbade Josefina from ever seeing Cervantes again, perhaps because of the young man's poor prospects of ever rising from poverty—Miguel's own father was embargoed for debt. The court records of the proceedings show a very poor household. While some of his biographers argue that he studied at the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">
        University of Salamanca
       </a>
       , there is no solid evidence for supposing that he did so.
       <sup class="reference" id="ref_Cnone">
        <a href="#endnote_Cnone">
         [c]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There has been speculation also that Cervantes studied with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
        Jesuits
       </a>
       in Córdoba or Seville.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Am_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Am-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       His siblings were Andrés (1543), Andrea (1544), Luisa (1546), Rodrigo (1550), Magdalena (1554) and Juan—known solely because he is mentioned in his father's will.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military_service_and_captivity">
        Military service and captivity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Military service and captivity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2662" data-file-width="2119" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg/170px-The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg/255px-The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg/340px-The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_Lepanto_by_Paolo_Veronese.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <i>
          Battle of Lepanto
         </i>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Veronese" title="Paolo Veronese">
          Paolo Veronese
         </a>
         (c. 1572, oil on canvas, 169 x 137 cm,
         <a href="/wiki/Gallerie_dell%27Accademia" title="Gallerie dell'Accademia">
          Gallerie dell'Accademia
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">
          Venice
         </a>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="332" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg/170px-Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg/255px-Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e8/Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nafpaktos_evlahos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Statue of Miguel de Cervantes at the harbour of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naupactus" title="Naupactus">
          Naupactus
         </a>
         (Lepanto)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The reasons that forced Cervantes to leave Spain remain uncertain. Possible reasons include that he was a "student" of the same name, a "sword-wielding fugitive from justice", or fleeing from a royal warrant of arrest, for having wounded a certain Antonio de Sigura in a duel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Like many young Spanish men who wanted to further their careers, Cervantes left for Italy. In Rome, he focused his attention on
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </a>
       art, architecture, and poetry – knowledge of
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_literature" title="Italian literature">
        Italian literature
       </a>
       is discernible in his work. He found "a powerful impetus to revive the contemporary world in light of its accomplishments".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ar32_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ar32-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thus, Cervantes' stay in Italy, as revealed in his later works, might be in part a desire for a return to an earlier period of the Renaissance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ar33_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ar33-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 1570, Cervantes had enlisted as a soldier in a regiment of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy_Marines" title="Spanish Navy Marines">
        Spanish Navy Marines
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Infantería de Marina
       </i>
       , stationed in Naples, then a possession of the Spanish crown. He was there for about a year before he saw active service. In September 1571, Cervantes sailed on board the
       <i>
        Marquesa
       </i>
       , part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">
        galley
       </a>
       fleet of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">
        Holy League
       </a>
       (a coalition of
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_V" title="Pope Pius V">
        Pope Pius V
       </a>
       , Spain, the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">
        Republic of Venice
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">
        Republic of Genoa
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Savoy" title="Duchy of Savoy">
        Duchy of Savoy
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">
        Knights Hospitaller
       </a>
       based in
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       , and others, under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        Philip II of Spain
       </a>
       's illegitimate half brother,
       <a href="/wiki/John_of_Austria" title="John of Austria">
        John of Austria
       </a>
       ) that defeated the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman
       </a>
       fleet on October 7 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">
        Battle of Lepanto
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Patras" title="Gulf of Patras">
        Gulf of Patras
       </a>
       . Though taken down with fever, Cervantes refused to stay below and asked to be allowed to take part in the battle, saying he would rather die for his God and his king than keep under cover. He fought on board a vessel and received three gunshot wounds – two in the chest and one which rendered his left arm useless. In
       <i>
        Journey to Parnassus
       </i>
       he was to say that he "had lost the movement of the left hand for the glory of the right" (referring to the success of the first part of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       ). Cervantes looked back on his conduct in the battle with pride: he believed he had taken part in an event that shaped the course of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_history" title="European history">
        European history
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       After the Battle of Lepanto, Cervantes remained in hospital in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Messina,_Italy" title="Messina, Italy">
        Messina, Italy
       </a>
       , for about six months, before his wounds healed enough to allow his joining the colours again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OrFiK_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OrFiK-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From 1572 to 1575, based mainly in Naples, he continued his soldier's life: he participated in expeditions to
       <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">
        Corfu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pylos" title="Pylos">
        Navarino
       </a>
       , and saw the fall of
       <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">
        Tunis
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/La_Goulette" title="La Goulette">
        La Goulette
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">
        Turks
       </a>
       in 1574.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcés_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcés-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         220
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 6 or 7 September 1575, Cervantes set sail on the
       <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">
        galley
       </a>
       <i>
        Sol
       </i>
       from Naples to
       <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
        Barcelona
       </a>
       , with letters of commendation to the king from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duque_de_Sessa" title="Duque de Sessa">
        Duke of Sessa
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-F41_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-F41-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the morning of 26 September, as the
       <i>
        Sol
       </i>
       approached the Catalan coast, it was attacked by Ottoman pirates and he was taken to Algiers, which had become one of the main and most cosmopolitan cities of the Ottoman Empire, and was kept there in captivity between the years of 1575 and 1580.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After five years as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">
        slave
       </a>
       in Algiers, and four unsuccessful escape attempts, he was ransomed by his parents and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinitarians" title="Trinitarians">
        Trinitarians
       </a>
       and returned to his family in Madrid. Not surprisingly, this traumatic period of Cervantes' life supplied subject matter for several of his literary works, notably the Captive's tale in
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       and the two plays set in Algiers –
       <i>
        El trato de Argel
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Life in Algiers
       </i>
       ) and
       <i>
        Los baños de Argel
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        The Dungeons of Algiers
       </i>
       ) – as well as episodes in a number of other writings, although never in straight autobiographical form.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life">
        Later life
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later life">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1421" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg/220px-Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg/330px-Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg/440px-Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_de_Cervantes_at_the_National_Library.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "The pen is the language of the soul; as the concepts that in it are generated, such will be its writings." – Miguel de Cervantes at the
         <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Nacional_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Biblioteca Nacional de España">
          Biblioteca Nacional de España
         </a>
         (National Library of Spain).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Cervantes led a middle-class life after his return to Spain. Like almost all authors of his day, he was unable to support himself through his writings. Two periods of his life that are very well documented are his years of work in Andalucía as a purchasing agent for the Spanish navy (i.e., the King). This led to his imprisonment for a few months in Seville after a banker with whom he had deposited Crown funds went bankrupt. (Since Cervantes says that
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       was "engendered" in a prison, that is presumably a reference to this episode.) He also worked as a tax collector, travelling from town to town collecting back taxes due the crown. He applied unsuccessfully for "one of four vacant positions in the New World", one of them as an accountant for the port of
       <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">
        Cartagena
       </a>
       . At the time he was living in Valladolid, then briefly the capital (1601–1606), and finishing
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       Part One, he was presumably working in the banking industry, or a related occupation where his accounting skills could be put to use. He was turned down for a position as secretary to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Castro_y_Andrade" title="Pedro Fernández de Castro y Andrade">
        Pedro Fernández de Castro y Andrade
       </a>
       , the Count of Lemos, although he did receive some type of pension from him, which permitted him to write full-time during his final years (about 1610 to 1616). His last known written words – the dedication to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Trabajos_de_Persiles_y_Sigismunda" title="Los Trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda">
        Los Trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda
       </a>
       – were written, he tells us, after having received
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_Unction" title="Extreme Unction">
        Extreme Unction
       </a>
       . He died in 1616 of type II
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">
        diabetes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His burial place in Madrid was reportedly rediscovered in March 2015, but his unpublished manuscripts were mostly lost.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_pursuits">
        Literary pursuits
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Literary pursuits">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
        Don Quixote
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-essay-like" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           is written like a
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTESSAY" title="Wikipedia:NOTESSAY">
            personal reflection or opinion essay
           </a>
          </b>
          that states a Wikipedia editor's personal feelings about a topic.
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit">
            help improve it
           </a>
           by rewriting it in an
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Encyclopedic_style" title="Wikipedia:Encyclopedic style">
            encyclopedic style
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (March 2015)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="713" data-file-width="479" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg/170px-Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg/255px-Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg/340px-Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Don_Quijote_illustrated_by_Gustav_Dore_V.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Miguel de Cervantes's famous work, Don Quijote illustrated by Doré
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1421" data-file-width="1137" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg/170px-Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg/255px-Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg/340px-Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Don_Quijote_Illustration_by_Gustave_Dore_VII.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Another Don Quijote Illustration by Gustave Doré, this one is of the famous windmill scene
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Esquivias" title="Esquivias">
        Esquivias
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Toledo" title="Province of Toledo">
        Toledo
       </a>
       , on 12 December 1584, he married the much younger Catalina de Salazar y Palacios (born Esquivias – d. 31 October 1626),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       daughter of Fernando de Salazar y Vozmediano and Catalina de Palacios. Her uncle Alonso de Quesada y Salazar is said to have inspired the character of Don Quixote.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Over the next 20 years, Cervantes led a nomadic existence, working as a purchasing agent for the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">
        Spanish Armada
       </a>
       and as a tax collector. He suffered bankruptcy and was imprisoned at least twice (1597 and 1602) for irregularities in his accounts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Between 1596 and 1600, he lived primarily in Seville. In 1606, Cervantes settled in Madrid, where he remained for the rest of his life.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1585 Cervantes published his first major work,
       <i>
        La Galatea
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a pastoral romance, at the same time that some of his plays, now lost – except for
       <i>
        El trato de Argel
       </i>
       (where he dealt with the life of Christian slaves in Algiers) and
       <i>
        El cerco de Numancia
       </i>
       – were playing on the stages of Madrid.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <i>
        La Galatea
       </i>
       received little contemporary notice; and Cervantes never wrote the continuation for it, which he repeatedly promised to do. Cervantes next turned his attention to drama, hoping to derive an income from that source, but his plays failed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aside from his plays, his most ambitious work in verse was
       <i>
        Viage del Parnaso
       </i>
       (1614) – an allegory which consisted largely of a rather tedious though good-natured review of contemporary poets. Cervantes himself realized that he was deficient in poetic talent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       If a remark which Cervantes himself makes in the prologue of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       is to be taken literally, the idea of the work (though hardly the writing of its First Part, as some have maintained) occurred to him while in jail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cervantes' idea was to give a picture of real life and manners, and to express himself in clear language. The intrusion of everyday speech into a literary context was acclaimed by the reading public. The author stayed poor until January 1605, when the first part of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       appeared.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The popularity of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       led to the publication of an unauthorized continuation of it by an unknown writer,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who masqueraded under the name of
       <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Avellaneda" title="Alonso Fernández de Avellaneda">
        Alonso Fernández de Avellaneda
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cervantes produced his own continuation, or Second Part, of
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which made its appearance in 1615.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He had promised the publication of a second part in 1613 in the foreword to the
       <i>
        Novelas ejemplares
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Exemplary Novels
       </i>
       ), a year before the publication of Avellaneda's book.
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       has been regarded chiefly as a novel of purpose.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is stated again and again that he wrote it in order to satirize the
       <a href="/wiki/Chivalric_romance" title="Chivalric romance">
        chivalric romance
       </a>
       and to challenge the popularity of a form of literature that had been a favourite of the general public for more than a century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table cellspacing="5" class="toccolours" style="float: left; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 2em; font-size: 85%; background:#c6dbf7; color:black; width:30em; max-width: 40%;">
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align: left;">
         "What I cannot help taking amiss is that he
         <sup class="reference" id="ref_Dnone">
          <a href="#endnote_Dnone">
           [d]
          </a>
         </sup>
         charges me with being old and one-handed, as if it had been in my power to keep time from passing over me, or as if the loss of my hand had been brought about in some tavern, and not on the grandest occasion the past or present has seen, or the future can hope to see. If my wounds have no beauty to the beholder's eye, they are, at least, honourable in the estimation of those who know where they were received; for the soldier shows to greater advantage dead in battle than alive in flight."—from the Preface to Volume 2 of
         <i>
          Don Quixote
         </i>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
          <a href="#cite_note-29">
           [29]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <i>
        Don Quixote
       </i>
       certainly reveals much narrative power, considerable humour, a mastery of dialogue, and a forceful style. Of the two parts written by Cervantes,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       perhaps the first is the more popular with the general public – containing the famous episodes of the tilting at windmills, the attack on the flock of sheep, the vigil in the courtyard of the inn, and the episode with the barber and the shaving basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The second part shows more constructive insight, better delineation of character, improved style, and more realism and probability in its action.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most people agree that it is richer and more profound.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1613, he published a collection of tales,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <i>
        Exemplary Novels
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       some of which had been written earlier. The
       <a href="/wiki/Picaresque_novel" title="Picaresque novel">
        picaroon
       </a>
       strain, already made familiar in Spain through the Picaresque novels of
       <a href="/wiki/Lazarillo_de_Tormes" title="Lazarillo de Tormes">
        Lazarillo de Tormes
       </a>
       and his successors, appears in one or another of them, especially in the
       <i>
        Rinconete y Cortadillo
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1614, he published the
       <i>
        Viage del Parnaso
       </i>
       and in 1615, the
       <i>
        Eight Comedies and Eight New Interludes
       </i>
       . At the same time,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cervantes continued working on
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Trabajos_de_Persiles_y_Sigismunda" title="Los Trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda">
         Los Trabajos de Persiles y Sigismunda
        </a>
       </i>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_novel" title="Byzantine novel">
        novel of adventurous travel
       </a>
       , completed just before his death,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_27-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Catholic-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and appearing posthumously in January 1617.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Br_9-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-Br-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Death">
        Death
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Death">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trinitmad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1890" data-file-width="1417" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Trinitmad.jpg/220px-Trinitmad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Trinitmad.jpg/330px-Trinitmad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Trinitmad.jpg/440px-Trinitmad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trinitmad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cervantes was buried at the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convento_de_las_Monjas_Trinitarias_Descalzas" title="Convento de las Monjas Trinitarias Descalzas">
          Convent of the Barefoot Trinitarians
         </a>
         in Madrid
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Cervantes died in Madrid on 22 April 1616
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was buried the next day, 23 April.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The cause of his death, according to Antonio López Alonso, a modern physician who has examined the surviving documentation, was
       <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">
        type-2 diabetes
       </a>
       , a result of a
       <a href="/wiki/Cirrhosis" title="Cirrhosis">
        cirrhosis
       </a>
       of the liver. This is the best explanation for the intense thirst he complained of. The cirrhosis was not caused by alcoholism; Cervantes was too productive, especially in his final years, to have been an alcoholic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For many years 23 April 1616 was shown as the date of his death in some references, and is still the date on which his death is widely commemorated (along with that of
       <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">
        William Shakespeare
       </a>
       , although the date for Cervantes was according to the Gregorian calendar while the date for Shakespeare was according to the Julian calendar and therefore 10 days later in real time).
      </p>
      <p>
       In accordance with Cervantes' will, he was buried in the neighbouring
       <a href="/wiki/Convent_of_the_Barefoot_Trinitarians" title="Convent of the Barefoot Trinitarians">
        Convent of the Barefoot Trinitarians
       </a>
       , in central Madrid.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His bones went missing in 1673 when building work was done at the convent, and were known to have been taken to a different convent and returned later. A project promoted and led by
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_Prado" title="Fernando de Prado">
        Fernando de Prado
       </a>
       began in 2014 to rediscover his remains.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In January 2015, it was reported that researchers searching for Cervantes' remains had found part of a casket bearing his initials, MC, at the convent. Francisco Etxeberria, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forensic_anthropologist" title="Forensic anthropologist">
        forensic anthropologist
       </a>
       leading the search, said: "Remains of caskets were found, wood, rocks, some bone fragments, and indeed one of the fragments of a board of one of the caskets had the letters 'M.C.' formed in tacks." The first significant search for Cervantes' remains had been launched in May 2014 and had involved the use of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infrared_camera" title="Infrared camera">
        infrared cameras
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/3D_scanner" title="3D scanner">
        3D scanners
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ground-penetrating_radar" title="Ground-penetrating radar">
        ground-penetrating radar
       </a>
       . The team had identified 33 alcoves where bones could be stored.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 17 March 2015, it was reported that Cervantes' remains had been discovered, along with those of his wife and others, at the Convent of the Barefoot Trinitarians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Through documentary research, archaeologists stated that they had identified the remains as those of Cervantes. Clues from Cervantes' life, such as the loss of the use of his left hand at age 24 and the fact that he had taken at least one bullet to the chest, were hoped to help in the identification. Historian Fernando de Prado had spent more than four years trying to find funding before Madrid City Council had agreed to pay. DNA testing would now be carried out in an attempt to confirm the findings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 11 June 2015, Cervantes was given a formal burial at a Madrid convent, containing a monument holding bone fragments that were believed to have been the author's. The city mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Ana_Botella" title="Ana Botella">
        Ana Botella
       </a>
       and military attended the event.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Works">
        Works
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_de_Cervantes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Works">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
